</div></div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_reforms_and_sociopolitical_issues">Political reforms and sociopolitical issues</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Democratic_development_in_Hong_Kong" title="Democratic development in Hong Kong">Democratic development in Hong Kong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Hong_Kong" title="Human rights in Hong Kong">Human rights in Hong Kong</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:190616_HK_Protest_Incendo_03.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/190616_HK_Protest_Incendo_03.jpg/220px-190616_HK_Protest_Incendo_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/190616_HK_Protest_Incendo_03.jpg/330px-190616_HK_Protest_Incendo_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/190616_HK_Protest_Incendo_03.jpg/440px-190616_HK_Protest_Incendo_03.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:190616_HK_Protest_Incendo_03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%932020_Hong_Kong_protests" title="2019–2020 Hong Kong protests">2019–2020 Hong Kong protests</a></div></div></div>
<p>Hong Kong is governed by a <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_regime" title="Hybrid regime">hybrid regime</a> that is not fully <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative</a> of the population. Legislative Council members elected by functional constituencies composed of professional and special interest groups are accountable to these narrow corporate electorates and not the general public. This electoral arrangement has guaranteed a pro-establishment majority in the legislature since the transfer of sovereignty. Similarly, the chief executive is selected by establishment politicians and corporate members of the Election Committee rather than directly elected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hybridregime_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-hybridregime-152">[146]</a></sup> Although <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> for the chief executive and all Legislative Council elections are defined goals of Basic Law <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Basic_Law_Article_45" title="Hong Kong Basic Law Article 45">Articles 45</a> and 68,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[147]</a></sup> the legislature is only partially directly elected, and the executive continues to be nominated by an unrepresentative body.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hybridregime_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-hybridregime-152">[146]</a></sup> The government has been repeatedly petitioned to introduce direct elections for these positions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[149]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ethnic minorities (except those of European ancestry) have marginal representation in government and often experience discrimination in housing, education, and employment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[151]</a></sup> Employment vacancies and public service appointments frequently have language requirements which minority job seekers do not meet, and language education resources remain inadequate for Chinese learners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[153]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Foreign_domestic_helpers_in_Hong_Kong" title="Foreign domestic helpers in Hong Kong">Foreign domestic helpers</a>, predominantly women from the Philippines and Indonesia, have little protection under regional law. Although they live and work in Hong Kong, these workers are not treated as ordinary residents and are ineligible for right of abode in the territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[154]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sex_trafficking_in_Hong_Kong" title="Sex trafficking in Hong Kong">Sex trafficking in Hong Kong</a> is an issue. Hongkonger and foreign women and girls are forced into <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_Hong_Kong" title="Prostitution in Hong Kong">prostitution</a> in brothels, homes, and businesses in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Joint Declaration guarantees the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basic_Law_of_Hong_Kong" title="Basic Law of Hong Kong">Basic Law of Hong Kong</a> for 50 years after the transfer of sovereignty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carroll181_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-Carroll181-91">[85]</a></sup> It does not specify how Hong Kong will be governed after 2047, and the central government's role in determining the territory's future system of government is the subject of political debate and speculation. Hong Kong's political and judicial systems may be integrated with China's at that time, or the territory may continue to be administered separately.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[160]</a></sup> However, in response to <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%932020_Hong_Kong_protests" title="2019–2020 Hong Kong protests">large-scale protests in 2019 and 2020</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Standing_Committee_of_the_National_People%27s_Congress" title="Standing Committee of the National People's Congress">Standing Committee of the National People's Congress</a> passed the controversial <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_national_security_law" title="Hong Kong national security law">Hong Kong national security law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[161]</a></sup> The law criminalises secession, subversion, terrorism and collusion with foreign elements and establishes the Office for Safeguarding National Security of the CPG in the HKSAR, an investigative office under Central People's Government authority immune from HKSAR jurisdiction. Some of the aforementioned acts were previously considered protected speech under Hong Kong law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NPC_Observer_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-NPC_Observer-130">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[162]</a></sup> The United Kingdom considers the law to be a serious violation of the Joint Declaration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[163]</a></sup> In October 2020, Hong Kong police arrested seven pro-<a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> politicians over tussles with pro-Beijing politicians in the Legislative Council in May. They were charged with contempt and interfering with members of the council, while none of the pro-Beijing lawmakers were detained.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[164]</a></sup> Annual commemorations of the <a href="/wiki/1989_Tiananmen_Square_protests_and_massacre" title="1989 Tiananmen Square protests and massacre">1989 Tiananmen Square protests and massacre</a> were also cancelled amidst fears of violating the national security law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[165]</a></sup> In March 2021, the Chinese central government unilaterally <a href="/wiki/2021_Hong_Kong_electoral_changes" title="2021 Hong Kong electoral changes">changed Hong Kong's electoral system</a> and established the <a href="/wiki/Candidate_Eligibility_Review_Committee" title="Candidate Eligibility Review Committee">Candidate Eligibility Review Committee</a>, which would be tasked with screening and evaluating political candidates for their "patriotism".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-france2420210311_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-france2420210311-108">[102]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Hong_Kong" title="Geography of Hong Kong">Geography of Hong Kong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environment_of_Hong_Kong" title="Environment of Hong Kong">Environment of Hong Kong</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hong_Kong,_China.jpg"><img alt="Satellite image showing areas of vegetation and conurbation." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Hong_Kong%2C_China.jpg/220px-Hong_Kong%2C_China.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Hong_Kong%2C_China.jpg/330px-Hong_Kong%2C_China.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Hong_Kong%2C_China.jpg/440px-Hong_Kong%2C_China.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hong_Kong,_China.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Areas of urban development and vegetation are visible in this satellite image.</div></div></div>
<p>Hong Kong is on China's southern coast, 60 km (37 mi) east of Macau, on the east side of the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_River_Delta" title="Pearl River Delta">Pearl River estuary</a>. It is surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a> on all sides except the north, which neighbours the <a href="/wiki/Guangdong" title="Guangdong">Guangdong</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen" title="Shenzhen">Shenzhen</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Sham_Chun_River" title="Sham Chun River">Sham Chun River</a>. The territory's 1,110.18 km<sup>2</sup> (428.64 sq mi)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-172">[166]</a></sup> area (2754.97 km<sup>2</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_172-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-172">[166]</a></sup> if the maritime area is included) consists of <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Island" title="Hong Kong Island">Hong Kong Island</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kowloon_Peninsula" title="Kowloon Peninsula">Kowloon Peninsula</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_Territories" title="New Territories">New Territories</a>, Lantau Island, and over 200 other islands. Of the total area, 1,073 km<sup>2</sup> (414 sq mi) is land and 35 km<sup>2</sup> (14 sq mi) is water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-cia-42">[36]</a></sup> The territory's highest point is <a href="/wiki/Tai_Mo_Shan" title="Tai Mo Shan">Tai Mo Shan</a>, 957 metres (3,140 ft) above sea level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[167]</a></sup> Urban development is concentrated on the Kowloon Peninsula, Hong Kong Island, and in <a href="/wiki/New_towns_of_Hong_Kong" title="New towns of Hong Kong">new towns</a> throughout the New Territories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[168]</a></sup> Much of this is built on <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation_in_Hong_Kong" title="Land reclamation in Hong Kong">reclaimed land</a>; 70 km<sup>2</sup> (27 sq mi) (6% of the total land or about 25% of developed space in the territory) is reclaimed from the sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reclamation_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-reclamation-175">[169]</a></sup>
</p><p>Undeveloped terrain is hilly to mountainous, with very little flat land, and consists mostly of grassland, woodland, shrubland, or farmland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[171]</a></sup> About 40% of the remaining land area is <a href="/wiki/Conservation_in_Hong_Kong" title="Conservation in Hong Kong">country parks</a> and nature reserves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[172]</a></sup> The territory has a diverse ecosystem; over 3,000 species of <a href="/wiki/Vascular_plant" title="Vascular plant">vascular plants</a> occur in the region (300 of which are native to Hong Kong), and thousands of insect, avian, and marine species.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[174]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>
<p>Hong Kong has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a> <i>Cwa</i>), characteristic of southern China, despite being located south of the <a href="/wiki/Tropic_of_Cancer" title="Tropic of Cancer">Tropic of Cancer</a>. Summer is hot and humid, with occasional showers and thunderstorms and warm air from the southwest. <a href="/wiki/Typhoon" title="Typhoon">Typhoons</a> occur most often then, sometimes resulting in floods or landslides. Winters are mild and usually sunny at the beginning, becoming cloudy towards February. Frequent cold fronts bring strong, cooling winds from the north and occasionally result in chilly weather. Autumn is the sunniest season, whilst spring is generally cloudy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HKClimate_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-HKClimate-181">[175]</a></sup> When there is snowfall, which is extremely rare, it is usually at high elevations. Hong Kong averages 1,709 hours of sunshine per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[176]</a></sup> Historic temperature extremes at the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory" title="Hong Kong Observatory">Hong Kong Observatory</a> are 36.6 °C (97.9 °F) on 22 August 2017 and 0.0 °C (32.0 °F) on 18 January 1893.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[177]</a></sup> The highest and lowest recorded temperatures in all of Hong Kong are 39.0 °C (102 °F) at <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Wetland_Park" title="Hong Kong Wetland Park">Wetland Park</a> on 22 August 2017,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[178]</a></sup> and −6.0 °C (21.2 °F) at Tai Mo Shan <a href="/wiki/January_2016_East_Asia_cold_wave" title="January 2016 East Asia cold wave">on 24 January 2016</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[179]</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Hong_Kong" title="Architecture of Hong Kong">Architecture of Hong Kong</a></div><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Montane_Mansion_Quarry_Bay.B.JPG"><img alt="Tall blocks of flats, attached on three sides" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Montane_Mansion_Quarry_Bay.B.JPG/220px-Montane_Mansion_Quarry_Bay.B.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Montane_Mansion_Quarry_Bay.B.JPG/330px-Montane_Mansion_Quarry_Bay.B.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Montane_Mansion_Quarry_Bay.B.JPG/440px-Montane_Mansion_Quarry_Bay.B.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Montane_Mansion_Quarry_Bay.B.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A residential building in <a href="/wiki/Quarry_Bay" title="Quarry Bay">Quarry Bay</a></div></div></div>
<p>Hong Kong has the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_with_the_most_skyscrapers" title="List of cities with the most skyscrapers">largest number of skyscrapers</a>, with 482 towers taller than 150 metres (490 ft),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SkyscraperCenter_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-SkyscraperCenter-43">[37]</a></sup> and the third-largest number of high-rise buildings in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[183]</a></sup> The lack of available space restricted development to high-density residential <a href="/wiki/Tenement" title="Tenement">tenements</a> and commercial complexes packed closely together on buildable land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[184]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Single-family_detached_home" title="Single-family detached home">Single-family detached homes</a> are uncommon and generally only found in outlying areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[185]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/International_Commerce_Centre" title="International Commerce Centre">International Commerce Centre</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Finance_Centre_(Hong_Kong)" title="International Finance Centre (Hong Kong)">Two International Finance Centre</a> are the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_Hong_Kong" title="List of tallest buildings in Hong Kong">tallest buildings in Hong Kong</a> and are among the tallest in the Asia-Pacific region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[186]</a></sup> Other distinctive buildings lining the Hong Kong Island skyline include the <a href="/wiki/HSBC_Building_(Hong_Kong)" title="HSBC Building (Hong Kong)">HSBC Main Building</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Anemometer" title="Anemometer">anemometer</a>-topped triangular <a href="/wiki/Central_Plaza_(Hong_Kong)" title="Central Plaza (Hong Kong)">Central Plaza</a>, the circular <a href="/wiki/Hopewell_Centre_(Hong_Kong)" title="Hopewell Centre (Hong Kong)">Hopewell Centre</a>, and the sharp-edged <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_China_Tower_(Hong_Kong)" title="Bank of China Tower (Hong Kong)">Bank of China Tower</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FengShui_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-FengShui-194">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[188]</a></sup>
</p><p>Demand for new construction has contributed to frequent demolition of older buildings, freeing space for modern high-rises.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[189]</a></sup> However, many examples of European and <a href="/wiki/Lingnan_architecture" title="Lingnan architecture">Lingnan architecture</a> are still found throughout the territory. Older government buildings are examples of colonial architecture. The 1846 <a href="/wiki/Flagstaff_House" title="Flagstaff House">Flagstaff House</a>, the former residence of the commanding British military officer, is the oldest Western-style building in Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[190]</a></sup> Some (including the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Final_Appeal_Building" title="Court of Final Appeal Building">Court of Final Appeal Building</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Observatory" title="Hong Kong Observatory">Hong Kong Observatory</a>) retain their original function, and others have been <a href="/wiki/Adaptive_reuse" title="Adaptive reuse">adapted and reused</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Former_Marine_Police_Headquarters" title="Former Marine Police Headquarters">Former Marine Police Headquarters</a> was redeveloped into a commercial and retail complex,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TourismFacts_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-TourismFacts-198">[191]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9thanie_(Hong_Kong)" title="Béthanie (Hong Kong)">Béthanie</a> (built in 1875 as a <a href="/wiki/Sanatorium" title="Sanatorium">sanatorium</a>) houses the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Academy_for_Performing_Arts" title="Hong Kong Academy for Performing Arts">Hong Kong Academy for Performing Arts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[192]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tin_Hau_Temple,_Joss_House_Bay" title="Tin Hau Temple, Joss House Bay">Tin Hau Temple</a>, dedicated to the sea goddess <a href="/wiki/Mazu" title="Mazu">Mazu</a> (originally built in 1012 and rebuilt in 1266), is the territory's oldest existing structure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[193]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ping_Shan_Heritage_Trail" title="Ping Shan Heritage Trail">Ping Shan Heritage Trail</a> has architectural examples of several imperial Chinese dynasties, including the <a href="/wiki/Tsui_Sing_Lau_Pagoda" title="Tsui Sing Lau Pagoda">Tsui Sing Lau Pagoda</a> (Hong Kong's only remaining pagoda).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[194]</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Tong_lau" title="Tong lau">Tong lau</a></i>, mixed-use tenement buildings constructed during the colonial era, blended southern Chinese architectural styles with European influences. These were especially prolific during the immediate post-war period, when many were rapidly built to house large numbers of Chinese migrants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[195]</a></sup> Examples include <a href="/wiki/Lui_Seng_Chun" title="Lui Seng Chun">Lui Seng Chun</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Blue_House_(Hong_Kong)" title="Blue House (Hong Kong)">Blue House</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wan_Chai" title="Wan Chai">Wan Chai</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Nos._600%E2%80%93626_Shanghai_Street" title="Nos. 600–626 Shanghai Street">Shanghai Street shophouses</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mong_Kok" title="Mong Kok">Mong Kok</a>. Mass-produced <a href="/wiki/Public_housing_in_Hong_Kong" title="Public housing in Hong Kong">public-housing estates</a>, built since the 1960s, are mainly constructed in <a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">modernist style</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[196]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1158px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hong_Kong_at_night.jpg" title="The Hong Kong Island skyline, viewed from the Victoria Harbour waterfront"><img alt="Skyline at night, with building lights reflected in water" data-file-height="948" data-file-width="4481" decoding="async" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Hong_Kong_at_night.jpg/1150px-Hong_Kong_at_night.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Hong_Kong_at_night.jpg/1725px-Hong_Kong_at_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Hong_Kong_at_night.jpg/2300px-Hong_Kong_at_night.jpg 2x" width="1150"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hong_Kong_at_night.jpg" title="File:Hong Kong at night.jpg"> </a></div>The Hong Kong Island skyline, viewed from the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Harbour" title="Victoria Harbour">Victoria Harbour</a> waterfront</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1608px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kowloon_Panorama_by_Ryan_Cheng_2010.jpg" title="City view of Kowloon, Hong Kong Island, and the Hong Kong skyline"><img alt="" data-file-height="785" data-file-width="5562" decoding="async" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Kowloon_Panorama_by_Ryan_Cheng_2010.jpg/1600px-Kowloon_Panorama_by_Ryan_Cheng_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Kowloon_Panorama_by_Ryan_Cheng_2010.jpg/2400px-Kowloon_Panorama_by_Ryan_Cheng_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Kowloon_Panorama_by_Ryan_Cheng_2010.jpg/3200px-Kowloon_Panorama_by_Ryan_Cheng_2010.jpg 2x" width="1600"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kowloon_Panorama_by_Ryan_Cheng_2010.jpg" title="File:Kowloon Panorama by Ryan Cheng 2010.jpg"> </a></div>City view of Kowloon, Hong Kong Island, and the Hong Kong skyline</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Hong_Kong" title="Demographics of Hong Kong">Demographics of Hong Kong</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_people" title="Hong Kong people">Hong Kong people</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Hongkong_2016.png"><img alt="Population graph" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="610" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Hongkong_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Hongkong_2016.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Hongkong_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Hongkong_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Hongkong_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Hongkong_2016.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Hongkong_2016.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2016 <a href="/wiki/Population_pyramid" title="Population pyramid">population pyramid</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Census_and_Statistics_Department_(Hong_Kong)" title="Census and Statistics Department (Hong Kong)">Census and Statistics Department</a> estimated Hong Kong's population at 7,482,500 in mid-2019. The overwhelming majority (92%) is <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Han Chinese</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demographics_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-8">[6]</a></sup> most of whom are <a href="/wiki/Sze_Yap_people_in_Hong_Kong" title="Sze Yap people in Hong Kong">Taishanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Teochew_people" title="Teochew people">Teochew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hakka_people" title="Hakka people">Hakka</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_people" title="Cantonese people">Cantonese peoples</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[197]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[199]</a></sup> The remaining 8% are non-ethnic Chinese minorities, primarily <a href="/wiki/Filipinos_in_Hong_Kong" title="Filipinos in Hong Kong">Filipinos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesians_in_Hong_Kong" title="Indonesians in Hong Kong">Indonesians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_Asians_in_Hong_Kong" title="South Asians in Hong Kong">South Asians</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-demographics_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-demographics-8">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[200]</a></sup> However, most Filipinos and Indonesians in Hong Kong are short-term workers. According to a 2016 thematic report by the Hong Kong government, after excluding foreign domestic helpers, the real number of non-Chinese ethnic minorities in the city was 263,593, or 3.6% of Hong Kong's population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[201]</a></sup> About half the population have <a href="/wiki/British_nationality_law" title="British nationality law">some form of British nationality</a>, a legacy of colonial rule; 3.4 million residents have <a href="/wiki/British_National_(Overseas)" title="British National (Overseas)">British National (Overseas)</a> status, and 260,000 British citizens live in the territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[202]</a></sup> The vast majority also hold <a href="/wiki/Chinese_nationality_law" title="Chinese nationality law">Chinese nationality</a>, automatically granted to all ethnic Chinese residents at the transfer of sovereignty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[203]</a></sup> Headline <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> exceeds 7,060 people/km<sup>2</sup>, and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population_density" title="List of countries and dependencies by population density">fourth-highest</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[204]</a></sup>
</p><p>The predominant language is <a href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Cantonese</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Varieties_of_Chinese" title="Varieties of Chinese">variety of Chinese</a> originating in Guangdong. It is spoken by 94.6% of the population, 88.9% as a first language and 5.7% as a second language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016By-CensusLanguages_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-2016By-CensusLanguages-3">[3]</a></sup> Slightly over half the population (53.2%) speaks English, the other official language;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OfficialLanguagesOrd_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-OfficialLanguagesOrd-2">[2]</a></sup> 4.3% are native speakers, and 48.9% speak English as a second language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016By-CensusLanguages_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-2016By-CensusLanguages-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Code-switching_in_Hong_Kong" title="Code-switching in Hong Kong">Code-switching</a>, mixing English and Cantonese in informal conversation, is common among the bilingual population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[205]</a></sup> Post-handover governments have promoted <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin</a>, which is currently about as prevalent as English; 48.6% of the population speak Mandarin, with 1.9% native speakers and 46.7% as a second language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016By-CensusLanguages_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-2016By-CensusLanguages-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">Traditional Chinese characters</a> are used in writing, rather than the <a href="/wiki/Simplified_Chinese_characters" title="Simplified Chinese characters">simplified characters</a> used on the mainland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[206]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sik_Sik_Yuen_Wong_Tai_Sin_Temple_(1944336752).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Sik_Sik_Yuen_Wong_Tai_Sin_Temple_%281944336752%29.jpg/220px-Sik_Sik_Yuen_Wong_Tai_Sin_Temple_%281944336752%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Sik_Sik_Yuen_Wong_Tai_Sin_Temple_%281944336752%29.jpg/330px-Sik_Sik_Yuen_Wong_Tai_Sin_Temple_%281944336752%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Sik_Sik_Yuen_Wong_Tai_Sin_Temple_%281944336752%29.jpg/440px-Sik_Sik_Yuen_Wong_Tai_Sin_Temple_%281944336752%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sik_Sik_Yuen_Wong_Tai_Sin_Temple_(1944336752).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wong_Tai_Sin_Temple_(Hong_Kong)" title="Wong Tai Sin Temple (Hong Kong)">Wong Tai Sin Temple</a> is dedicated to the <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoist</a> deity <a href="/wiki/Wong_Tai_Sin" title="Wong Tai Sin">Wong Tai Sin</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Among the religious population, the traditional "<a href="/wiki/Three_teachings" title="Three teachings">three teachings</a>" of China, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Buddhism" title="Chinese Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a>, have the most adherents (20%), followed by <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> (12%) and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (4%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religionFacts_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-religionFacts-214">[207]</a></sup> Followers of other religions, including <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, generally originate from regions where their religion predominates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-religionFacts_214-1"><a href="#cite_note-religionFacts-214">[207]</a></sup>
</p><p>Life expectancy in Hong Kong was 82.38 years for males and 88.17 years for females in 2022, the highest in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[208]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">Cancer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">heart disease</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cerebrovascular_disease" title="Cerebrovascular disease">cerebrovascular disease</a>, and accidents are the territory's five leading causes of death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2017HealthFacts_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-2017HealthFacts-216">[209]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal public healthcare system</a> is funded by general-tax revenue, and treatment is highly subsidised; on average, 95% of healthcare costs are covered by the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[210]</a></sup>
</p><p>Income inequality has risen since the transfer of sovereignty, as the region's ageing population has gradually added to the number of nonworking people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[211]</a></sup> Although median household income steadily increased during the decade to 2016, the wage gap remained high;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IncomeDistribution_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-IncomeDistribution-219">[212]</a></sup> the 90th percentile of earners receive 41% of all income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IncomeDistribution_219-1"><a href="#cite_note-IncomeDistribution-219">[212]</a></sup> The city has the most billionaires per capita, with one billionaire per 109,657 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[213]</a></sup> Despite government efforts to reduce the growing disparity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[214]</a></sup> median income for the top 10% of earners is 44 times that of the bottom 10%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[215]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[216]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Hong_Kong" title="Economy of Hong Kong">Economy of Hong Kong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Hong_Kong" title="Tourism in Hong Kong">Tourism in Hong Kong</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kwai_Tsing_Container_Terminals.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Kwai_Tsing_Container_Terminals.jpg/220px-Kwai_Tsing_Container_Terminals.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Kwai_Tsing_Container_Terminals.jpg/330px-Kwai_Tsing_Container_Terminals.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Kwai_Tsing_Container_Terminals.jpg/440px-Kwai_Tsing_Container_Terminals.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kwai_Tsing_Container_Terminals.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Hong_Kong" title="Port of Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> is one of the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_container_ports" title="List of busiest container ports">busiest container ports</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hong_Kong_Product_Exports_(2019).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="715" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Hong_Kong_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/290px-Hong_Kong_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Hong_Kong_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/435px-Hong_Kong_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Hong_Kong_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg/580px-Hong_Kong_Product_Exports_%282019%29.svg.png 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hong_Kong_Product_Exports_(2019).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A proportional representation of Hong Kong exports, 2019</div></div></div>
<p>Hong Kong has a capitalist <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed</a> service economy, characterised by <a href="/wiki/Taxation_in_Hong_Kong" title="Taxation in Hong Kong">low taxation</a>, minimal government market intervention, and an established international financial market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[217]</a></sup> It is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">35th-largest economy</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">nominal GDP</a> of approximately US$373 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMFWEOHK_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-IMFWEOHK-15">[13]</a></sup> Hong Kong's economy ranked at the top of <a href="/wiki/The_Heritage_Foundation" title="The Heritage Foundation">the Heritage Foundation</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Economic_freedom" title="Economic freedom">economic freedom</a> index between 1995 and 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[218]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[219]</a></sup> However, Hong Kong was removed from the index by the Heritage Foundation in 2021, with the Foundation citing a "loss of political freedom and autonomy<span class="nowrap"> </span>... [making Hong Kong] almost indistinguishable in many respects from other major Chinese commercial centers like Shanghai and Beijing".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[220]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Stock_Exchange" title="Hong Kong Stock Exchange">Hong Kong Stock Exchange</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_stock_exchanges" title="List of stock exchanges">seventh-largest in the world</a>, with a market capitalisation of HK$30.4 trillion (US$3.87 trillion) as of December 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hong_Kong&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[221]</a></sup> Hong Kong is ranked as the 14th most innovative territory in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index" title="Global Innovation Index">Global Innovation Index</a> in 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[222]</a></sup> The city is sometimes referred to as "Silicon Harbor",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tech_Monitor_1999_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tech_Monitor_1999-230">[223]</a></sup> a nickname derived from <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a> in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>. Hong Kong hosts several <a href="/wiki/High_tech" title="High tech">high tech</a> and <a href="/wiki/Innovation" title="Innovation">innovation</a> companies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rohwer_2001_p._168_231-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rohwer_2001_p._168-231">[224]</a></sup> including several multinational companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_1991_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_1991-232">[225]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cragg_1993_p._85_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cragg_1993_p._85-233">[226]</a></sup>
</p><p>Hong Kong is the tenth-largest trading entity in <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports" title="List of countries by exports">exports</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_imports" title="List of countries by imports">imports</a> (2017), trading more goods in value than its gross domestic product.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAExports_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIAExports-32">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIAImports_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIAImports-33">[27]</a></sup> Over half of its cargo throughput consists of <a href="/wiki/Transshipment" title="Transshipment">transshipments</a> (goods travelling through Hong Kong). Products from mainland China account for about 40% of that traffic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LegcoEconomy_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-LegcoEconomy-234">[227]</a></sup> The city's location allowed it to establish a transportation and logistics infrastructure which includes the world's seventh-busiest container port<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[228]</a></sup> and the busiest airport for international cargo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[229]</a></sup> The territory's largest export markets are mainland China and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_42-3"><a href="#cite_note-cia-42">[36]</a></sup> Hong Kong is a key part of the <a href="/wiki/21st_Century_Maritime_Silk_Road" title="21st Century Maritime Silk Road">21st Century Maritime Silk Road</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[230]</a></sup> It has little arable land and few natural resources, importing most of its food and raw materials. More than 90% of Hong Kong's food is imported, including nearly all of its meat and rice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[231]</a></sup> Agricultural activity is 0.1% of GDP and consists of growing premium food and flower varieties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[232]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although the territory had one of Asia's largest manufacturing economies during the latter half of the colonial era, Hong Kong's economy is now dominated by the service sector. The sector generates 92.7% of economic output, with the public sector accounting for about 10%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[233]</a></sup> Between 1961 and 1997 Hong Kong's gross domestic product increased by a factor of 180, and per capita GDP increased by a factor of 87.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[235]</a></sup> The territory's GDP relative to mainland China's peaked at 27% in 1993; it fell to less than 3% in 2017, as the mainland developed and liberalised its economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[236]</a></sup> Economic and infrastructure integration with China has increased significantly since the 1978 start of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_economic_reform" title="Chinese economic reform">market liberalisation</a> on the mainland. Since resumption of <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou%E2%80%93Kowloon_through_train" title="Guangzhou–Kowloon through train">cross-boundary train service</a> in 1979, many rail and road links have been improved and constructed, facilitating trade between regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[237]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HZMBridge_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-HZMBridge-245">[238]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mainland_and_Hong_Kong_Closer_Economic_Partnership_Arrangement" title="Mainland and Hong Kong Closer Economic Partnership Arrangement">Closer Economic Partnership Arrangement</a> formalised a policy of free trade between the two areas, with each jurisdiction pledging to remove remaining obstacles to trade and cross-boundary investment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MainlandCEPA_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-MainlandCEPA-246">[239]</a></sup> A similar economic partnership with Macau details the liberalisation of trade between the special administrative regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[240]</a></sup> Chinese companies have expanded their economic presence in the territory since the transfer of sovereignty. Mainland firms represent over half of the <a href="/wiki/Hang_Seng_Index" title="Hang Seng Index">Hang Seng Index</a> value, up from 5% in 1997.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[241]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[242]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hong_Kong_Exchange_Trade_Lobby_2007.jpg"><img alt="Large, empty room, with many desks and computer terminals" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Hong_Kong_Exchange_Trade_Lobby_2007.jpg/220px-Hong_Kong_Exchange_Trade_Lobby_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Hong_Kong_Exchange_Trade_Lobby_2007.jpg/330px-Hong_Kong_Exchange_Trade_Lobby_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Hong_Kong_Exchange_Trade_Lobby_2007.jpg/440px-Hong_Kong_Exchange_Trade_Lobby_2007.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hong_Kong_Exchange_Trade_Lobby_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former trading floor of the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Stock_Exchange" title="Hong Kong Stock Exchange">Hong Kong Stock Exchange</a></div></div></div>
<p>As the mainland liberalised its economy, Hong Kong's shipping industry faced intense competition from other Chinese ports. Half of China's trade goods were routed through Hong Kong in 1997, dropping to about 13% by 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Commons5R18_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-Commons5R18-250">[243]</a></sup> The territory's minimal taxation, common law system, and civil service attract overseas corporations wishing to establish a presence in Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Commons5R18_250-1"><a href="#cite_note-Commons5R18-250">[243]</a></sup> The city has the second-highest number of corporate headquarters in the Asia-Pacific region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[244]</a></sup> Hong Kong is a gateway for <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> in China, giving investors open access to mainland Chinese markets through direct links with <a href="/wiki/Shanghai-Hong_Kong_Stock_Connect" title="Shanghai-Hong Kong Stock Connect">the Shanghai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen-Hong_Kong_Stock_Connect" title="Shenzhen-Hong Kong Stock Connect">Shenzhen stock exchanges</a>. The territory was the first market outside mainland China for <a href="/wiki/Dim_sum_bond" title="Dim sum bond">renminbi-denominated bonds</a>, and is one of the largest hubs for offshore <a href="/wiki/Renminbi" title="Renminbi">renminbi</a> trading.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[245]</a></sup> In November 2020, Hong Kong's Financial Services and the Treasury Bureau proposed a new law that will restrict cryptocurrency trading to professional investors only, leaving amateur traders (93% of Hong Kong's trading population) out of the market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[246]</a></sup>
</p><p>The government has had a passive role in the economy. Colonial governments had little <a href="/wiki/Industrial_policy" title="Industrial policy">industrial policy</a> and implemented almost no <a href="/wiki/Trade_restriction" title="Trade restriction">trade controls</a>. Under the doctrine of "<a href="/wiki/Positive_non-interventionism" title="Positive non-interventionism">positive non-interventionism</a>", post-war administrations deliberately avoided the direct allocation of resources; active intervention was considered detrimental to economic growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ceo_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-ceo-254">[247]</a></sup> While the economy transitioned to a service basis during the 1980s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ceo_254-1"><a href="#cite_note-ceo-254">[247]</a></sup> late colonial governments introduced interventionist policies. Post-handover administrations continued and expanded these programmes, including <a href="/wiki/Export_credit_agency" title="Export credit agency">export-credit</a> guarantees, a <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_Provident_Fund" title="Mandatory Provident Fund">compulsory pension scheme</a>, a minimum wage, <a href="/wiki/Anti-discrimination_law" title="Anti-discrimination law">anti-discrimination laws</a>, and a state mortgage backer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EconomistEnd_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-EconomistEnd-255">[248]</a></sup>
</p><p>
Tourism is a major part of the economy, accounting for 5% of GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TourismFacts_198-1"><a href="#cite_note-TourismFacts-198">[191]</a></sup> In 2016, 26.6 million visitors contributed HK$258 billion (US$32.9 billion) to the territory, making Hong Kong the <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_rankings" title="World Tourism rankings">14th most popular destination for international tourists</a>. It is the most popular Chinese city for tourists, receiving over 70% more visitors than its closest competitor (Macau).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[249]</a></sup> The city is ranked as one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_cities_for_expatriate_employees" title="List of most expensive cities for expatriate employees">most expensive cities for expatriates</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[250]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[251]</a></sup> However, since 2020, there has been a sharp decline in incoming visitors due to tight COVID-19 travel restrictions. Additionally, due to the closure of Russian airspace in 2022, multiple airlines decided to cease their operations in Hong  Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[252]</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:808px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hong_Kong_Skyline_view_from_the_peak_2017.jpg" title="Victoria Peak is a major tourist attraction that offers views of Central and Victoria Harbour."><img alt="" data-file-height="8000" data-file-width="24000" decoding="async" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Hong_Kong_Skyline_view_from_the_peak_2017.jpg/800px-Hong_Kong_Skyline_view_from_the_peak_2017.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Hong_Kong_Skyline_view_from_the_peak_2017.jpg/1200px-Hong_Kong_Skyline_view_from_the_peak_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Hong_Kong_Skyline_view_from_the_peak_2017.jpg/1600px-Hong_Kong_Skyline_view_from_the_peak_2017.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hong_Kong_Skyline_view_from_the_peak_2017.jpg" title="File:Hong Kong Skyline view from the peak 2017.jpg"> </a></div><a href="/wiki/Victoria_Peak" title="Victoria Peak">Victoria Peak</a> is a major tourist attraction that offers views of <a href="/wiki/Central,_Hong_Kong" title="Central, Hong Kong">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Harbour" title="Victoria Harbour">Victoria Harbour</a>.</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Hong_Kong" title="Transport in Hong Kong">Transport in Hong Kong</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cross_Harbour_Tunnel_(1).JPG"><img alt="Tunnel entrance at night, with heavy traffic" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3056" data-file-width="4592" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Cross_Harbour_Tunnel_%281%29.JPG/220px-Cross_Harbour_Tunnel_%281%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Cross_Harbour_Tunnel_%281%29.JPG/330px-Cross_Harbour_Tunnel_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Cross_Harbour_Tunnel_%281%29.JPG/440px-Cross_Harbour_Tunnel_%281%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cross_Harbour_Tunnel_(1).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Cross-Harbour_Tunnel" title="Cross-Harbour Tunnel">Cross-Harbour Tunnel</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hung_Hom" title="Hung Hom">Hung Hom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kowloon" title="Kowloon">Kowloon</a></div></div></div>
<p>Hong Kong has a highly developed, sophisticated transport network. Over 90% of daily trips are made on public transport, the highest percentage in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pubtransport_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-pubtransport-44">[38]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Octopus_card" title="Octopus card">Octopus card</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Contactless_payment" title="Contactless payment">contactless</a> <a href="/wiki/Smart_card" title="Smart card">smart</a> <a href="/wiki/Digital_currency" title="Digital currency">payment</a> card, is widely accepted on railways, buses and ferries, and can be used for payment in most retail stores.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[253]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Peak_Tram" title="Peak Tram">Peak Tram</a>, Hong Kong's first public transport system, has provided <a href="/wiki/Funicular" title="Funicular">funicular</a> rail transport between <a href="/wiki/Central,_Hong_Kong" title="Central, Hong Kong">Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Peak" title="Victoria Peak">Victoria Peak</a> since 1888.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[254]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Western_District" title="Central and Western District">Central and Western District</a> has an extensive system of escalators and <a href="/wiki/Moving_walkway" title="Moving walkway">moving pavements</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Central%E2%80%93Mid-Levels_escalator" title="Central–Mid-Levels escalator">Mid-Levels escalator</a> (the world's longest outdoor covered escalator system).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[255]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Tramways" title="Hong Kong Tramways">Hong Kong Tramways</a> covers a portion of Hong Kong Island. The <a href="/wiki/MTR" title="MTR">Mass Transit Railway</a> (MTR) is an extensive passenger rail network, connecting 93 <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro</a> stations throughout the territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RailwayFacts_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-RailwayFacts-263">[256]</a></sup> With a daily ridership of over five million, the system serves 41% of all public transit passengers in the city<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LegcoTransport_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-LegcoTransport-264">[257]</a></sup> and has an on-time rate of 99.9%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[258]</a></sup> Cross-boundary train service to Shenzhen is offered by the <a href="/wiki/East_Rail_line" title="East Rail line">East Rail line</a>, and longer-distance <a href="/wiki/Inter-city_rail" title="Inter-city rail">inter-city trains</a> <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou%E2%80%93Kowloon_through_train" title="Guangzhou–Kowloon through train">to Guangzhou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai%E2%80%93Kowloon_through_train" title="Shanghai–Kowloon through train">Shanghai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Beijing%E2%80%93Kowloon_through_train" title="Beijing–Kowloon through train">Beijing</a> are operated from <a href="/wiki/Hung_Hom_station" title="Hung Hom station">Hung Hom station</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[259]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Express_Rail_Link" title="Hong Kong Express Rail Link">Connecting service</a> to the <a href="/wiki/China_Railway_High-speed" title="China Railway High-speed">national high-speed rail system</a> is provided at <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_West_Kowloon_railway_station" title="Hong Kong West Kowloon railway station">West Kowloon railway station</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[260]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although public transport systems handle most passenger traffic, there are over 500,000 private vehicles registered in Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[261]</a></sup> Automobiles drive <a href="/wiki/Left-_and_right-hand_traffic" title="Left- and right-hand traffic">on the left</a> (unlike in mainland China), because of historical influence of the British Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[262]</a></sup> Vehicle traffic is extremely congested in urban areas, exacerbated by limited space to expand roads and an increasing number of vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[263]</a></sup> More than 18,000 <a href="/wiki/Taxis_of_Hong_Kong" title="Taxis of Hong Kong">taxicabs</a>, easily identifiable by their bright colour, are licensed to carry riders in the territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[264]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bus_services_in_Hong_Kong" title="Bus services in Hong Kong">Bus services</a> operate more than 700 routes across the territory,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LegcoTransport_264-1"><a href="#cite_note-LegcoTransport-264">[257]</a></sup> with smaller <a href="/wiki/Public_light_bus" title="Public light bus">public light buses</a> (also known as minibuses) serving areas standard buses do not reach as frequently or directly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[265]</a></sup> Highways, organised with the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Strategic_Route_and_Exit_Number_System" title="Hong Kong Strategic Route and Exit Number System">Hong Kong Strategic Route and Exit Number System</a>, connect all major areas of the territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[266]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong%E2%80%93Zhuhai%E2%80%93Macau_Bridge" title="Hong Kong–Zhuhai–Macau Bridge">Hong Kong–Zhuhai–Macau Bridge</a> provides a direct route to the western side of the Pearl River estuary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HZMBridge_245-1"><a href="#cite_note-HZMBridge-245">[238]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:V813_entering_Sunny_Bay_Station_(20181013082946).jpg"><img alt="Light-rail train on a straightaway" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2905" data-file-width="4465" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/V813_entering_Sunny_Bay_Station_%2820181013082946%29.jpg/220px-V813_entering_Sunny_Bay_Station_%2820181013082946%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/V813_entering_Sunny_Bay_Station_%2820181013082946%29.jpg/330px-V813_entering_Sunny_Bay_Station_%2820181013082946%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/V813_entering_Sunny_Bay_Station_%2820181013082946%29.jpg/440px-V813_entering_Sunny_Bay_Station_%2820181013082946%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:V813_entering_Sunny_Bay_Station_(20181013082946).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>MTR train on the <a href="/wiki/Tung_Chung_line" title="Tung Chung line">Tung Chung line</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_International_Airport" title="Hong Kong International Airport">Hong Kong International Airport</a> is the territory's primary airport. Over 100 airlines operate flights from the airport, including locally based <a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a> (<a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a>), <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Airlines" title="Hong Kong Airlines">Hong Kong Airlines</a>, low-cost airline <a href="/wiki/HK_Express" title="HK Express">HK Express</a> and cargo airline <a href="/wiki/Air_Hong_Kong" title="Air Hong Kong">Air Hong Kong</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[267]</a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="List of busiest airports by passenger traffic">eighth-busiest airport by passenger traffic</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[268]</a></sup> and handles <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_cargo_traffic" title="List of busiest airports by cargo traffic">the most air-cargo traffic in the world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[269]</a></sup> Most private recreational aviation traffic flies through <a href="/wiki/Shek_Kong_Airfield" title="Shek Kong Airfield">Shek Kong Airfield</a>, under the supervision of the <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Aviation_Club" title="Hong Kong Aviation Club">Hong Kong Aviation Club</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[270]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Star_Ferry" title="Star Ferry">Star Ferry</a> operates two lines across Victoria Harbour for its 53,000 daily passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[271]</a></sup> Ferries also serve outlying islands inaccessible by other means. Smaller <a href="/wiki/Kai-to" title="Kai-to">kai-to</a> boats serve the most remote coastal settlements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[272]</a></sup> Ferry travel to Macau and mainland China is also available.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[273]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Junk_(ship)" title="Junk (ship)">Junks</a>, once common in Hong Kong waters, are no longer widely available and are used privately and for tourism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[274]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">Utilities</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Hong_Kong" title="Energy in Hong Kong">Energy in Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electricity_sector_in_Hong_Kong" title="Electricity sector in Hong Kong">Electricity sector in Hong Kong</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Hong_Kong" title="Water supply and sanitation in Hong Kong">Water supply and sanitation in Hong Kong</a></div>
<p>Hong Kong generates most of its electricity locally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-energystats2016p1_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-energystats2016p1-282">[275]</a></sup> The vast majority of this energy comes from fossil fuels, with 46% from coal and 47% from petroleum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[276]</a></sup> The rest is from other imports, including nuclear energy generated in mainland China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[277]</a></sup> Renewable sources account for a negligible amount of energy generated for the territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[278]</a></sup> Small-scale wind-power sources have been developed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-energystats2016p1_282-1"><a href="#cite_note-energystats2016p1-282">[275]</a></sup> and a small number of private homes and public buildings have installed solar panels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[279]</a></sup>
</p><p>With few natural lakes and rivers, high population density, inaccessible groundwater sources, and extremely seasonal rainfall, the territory does not have a reliable source of freshwater. The <a href="/wiki/Dong_River_(China)" title="Dong River (China)">Dongjiang River</a> in Guangdong supplies 70% of the city's water,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LeeWater_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-LeeWater-287">[280]</a></sup> and the remaining demand is filled by harvesting rainwater.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[281]</a></sup> Toilets in most built-up areas of the territory flush with seawater, greatly reducing freshwater use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LeeWater_287-1"><a href="#cite_note-LeeWater-287">[280]</a></sup>
</p><p>Broadband Internet access is widely available, with 92.6% of households connected. Connections over <a href="/wiki/Fiber_to_the_x" title="Fiber to the x">fibre-optic infrastructure</a> are increasingly prevalent,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[282]</a></sup> contributing to the high regional average connection speed of 21.9 Mbit/s (the world's fourth-fastest).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[283]</a></sup> Mobile-phone use is ubiquitous;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[284]</a></sup> there are more than 18 million <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_mobile_phones_in_use" title="List of countries by number of mobile phones in use">mobile-phone accounts</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[285]</a></sup> more than double the territory's population.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Hong_Kong" title="Culture of Hong Kong">Culture of Hong Kong</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Lingnan_culture" title="Lingnan culture">Lingnan culture</a></div>
<p>Hong Kong is characterised as a hybrid of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_world" title="Eastern world">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">West</a>. Traditional Chinese values emphasising family and education blend with Western ideals, including economic liberty and the rule of law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[286]</a></sup> Although the vast majority of the population is ethnically Chinese, Hong Kong has developed a distinct identity. The territory diverged from the mainland through its long period of colonial administration and a different pace of economic, social, and cultural development. Mainstream culture is derived from immigrants originating from various parts of China. This was influenced by British-style education, a separate political system, and the territory's rapid development during the late 20th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[287]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[288]</a></sup> Most migrants of that era fled poverty and war, reflected in the prevailing attitude toward wealth; Hongkongers tend to link self-image and decision-making to material benefits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[289]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[290]</a></sup> Residents' sense of local identity has markedly increased post-handover: The majority of the population (52%) identifies as "Hongkongers", while 11% describe themselves as "Chinese". The remaining population purport mixed identities, 23% as "Hongkonger in China" and 12% as "Chinese in Hong Kong".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[291]</a></sup>
</p><p>Traditional Chinese family values, including <a href="/wiki/Family_honor" title="Family honor">family honour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filial_piety" title="Filial piety">filial piety</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Sex_selection" title="Sex selection">preference for sons</a>, are prevalent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299">[292]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_family" title="Nuclear family">Nuclear families</a> are the most common households, although multi-generational and extended families are not unusual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[293]</a></sup> Spiritual concepts such as <i><a href="/wiki/Feng_shui" title="Feng shui">feng shui</a></i> are observed; large-scale construction projects often hire consultants to ensure proper building positioning and layout. The degree of its adherence to <i>feng shui</i> is believed to determine the success of a business.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FengShui_194-1"><a href="#cite_note-FengShui-194">[187]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Bagua" title="Bagua">Bagua</a></i> mirrors are regularly used to deflect evil spirits,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[294]</a></sup> and buildings often lack <a href="/wiki/Chinese_numerology" title="Chinese numerology">floor numbers with a 4</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[295]</a></sup> the number has a similar sound to the word for "die" in Cantonese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[296]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_cuisine" title="Hong Kong cuisine">Hong Kong cuisine</a></div>
